	- Have an event where people pay $X for you to ship out a box full of ingredients required to complete some recipe. This could be done on a monthly basis, and nobody leaves the table until their plat is clean.
	- Hi Mark, what I would really find useful is a primal carb lookup (with counter ideal) with highlights.
	- For example, you could type in a food eg. Boiled egg, and it would say 1.1g per egg – particulary high in Omega 3′s. Or type in Spinach, and it would say 3.0g per (100g) serving – good for iron.
	- Just nice and simple as either an app or a webpage. If a counter can be incorporated that would be great but it would require a sign in section to store your data.

		- Make it into an easy to use Iphone app and I would pay money for it. I know there are plenty of other calorie and Carb. counting options for apps out there, but one that pulls the best parts from the plethora of options, has online connectivity and trackers for friends and is specifically geared towards the primal way of eating would be great. I’d rather do my calorie and carb counting here, where if I were to eat healthy saturated fat I would be applauded rather than being told I am gong to die.
		- I would like to have an app for Omega 3 vs. Omega 6 lookups.
		- This. Absolutely. I use a food tracker on my iPhone and computer, but I would love one that is primally-centered. It would be great if it emphasized WHY a certain food is awesome (i.e. free-range, organic eggs are great for omegas). It would also be nice to be able to record exercises that count how much time we spend sprinting, lifting heavy things, and moving slowly.
	- Also, if the tracker could make suggestions for improvements. So, if my diet is low in vitamin C, it suggests what foods I can add to my diet to help make up the deficiency.
	- Another great feature would be a grocery list and recipe builder where I could lay out my meals for the week, which would build my grocery list, and it would let me know if I’m doing a good job of covering my nutritional needs.
	- Overall, just a food-tracker that gives more useful info beyond “calories in-calories out.”
	  collapsed:: true
		- YES! A primal focused app for my Android please. Look-up capability, food and fitness tracker and suggestions on food deficiency suggestions.
		- It would also be wonderful if you could type in the nutrient you are missing and it would make suggestions on what you could eat to get that nutrient. For instance, I need more potassium but not more bananas so what else could I eat?
		- An app would be great, but not just for nutrition. I think it would be handy to have one that tracked your activity as well. Let you plan HIIT workouts, have a Tabata type timer, and a GPS tracker to track your slow movement exercise (walking distance/ number of steps). It would be good to be able to upload and compare this with other Groksters. There are a multitude of apps that each do a bit of this, but it would be good to have one primal tracker to keep it all in the forefront of peoples minds.

	- Too little customer base (so prices would have to be higher), and no reason for it. I can get all my primal foods easily right in the supermarket (frozen greens and veggies, frozen chicken, cage-free eggs, etc.), and, as a bonus, feel totally virtuous as I walk past the cereal aisle with my nose in the air. Granted, my choices may not be for all (not organic or local or fresh enough), but paleo can’t encompass EVERY standard. standards tend to relax quite a bit once things become mainstream, such as “free-range” and “organic”…unfortunately.

	  collapsed:: true
		- Ditto on the vlogs. Multimedia is the way to go.
	- Short, easily digestible (no pun intended) YouTube videos on primal topics would be a big boon to our ‘awareness campaign’.
	- There’s minimal effort required for the viewer with videos compared to reading, adds a visual and audio component, videos are easily shared, easily embedded into other webpages and sites like YouTube already have built-in ranking systems so the more popular the videos become, the more likely people are to see them.
	- If a relative or a co-worker asks you why you don’t eat grains, you can just send ‘em a link to a video that explains why grains are terrible for you. They say that saturated fat or meat will kill you, send ‘em a link to a video that explains how and why that’s nonsense.
	- They’d have to be well-sourced, but the posts on MDA always are.

	- MarksDailyApple EXPANSION2
	- Over the years I’ve put together and given away numerous freebies (the 7-Day Course on the Fundamentals for Lifelong Health, the Primal Blueprint Fitness eBook, the Reader-Created Cookbooks and Primal Living in the Modern World to name a few), created new, handy web pages (the 101 page, the Recipe page, the Shopping List page, the Resource page and others), launched the forum, released a number of books, expanded the Primal supplement line, and began hosting events (Primal Transformation Seminars and PrimalCon) all with my stated goal in mind. Again, how can I help as many people as possible? How can I make this the best and most reader-friendly health site on the Interwebs? How can I best distill the science and make it easy to understand and practical to use? And how can I offer the best products and services a Grok or Grokette could want? While I don’t really need another project at the moment (I’m wrapping up two new books – The Primal Blueprint 90-Day Journal

	- I personally would like to see an article on food timing. For example, does it matter what part of the day you eat your carbs? I have heard theories that state that carbs make you sleepy through the tryptophan-serotonin-melatonin connection. Thus, if you wanted to be alert all day for work or school, eating carbs in the morning would be a bad idea. However, carbs for dinner (only fruits & tubers, of course) could potentially help you fall asleep – although I am not sure if they actually improve the quality of sleep. These are just theories I keep on hearing, what are your thoughts on this?

	- Hello Mark, I have not read all the comments on this thread, so what I say may have been said before. However, here are some of the things I would like to see more of on MDA :
	- * More in-depth articles, perhaps branching out to more esoteric subjects. I find that understanding the details about the science underlying the PB acts as great motivator to action.
	- * Following on from the previous point, the in-depth abstract articles could be supplemented by in-depth concrete articles about how to implement the PB lifestyle tangibly. This would mean more recipes, more workout ideas, etc. Calling out external resources or including guests posts on these topics would be a source of great variety.
	- * A more expansive “Ask Mark” section. Maybe doing the column bi-weekly instead of just once a week would be desirable. This would keep the blog interactive and more relevant to the readership.
	- I think MDA is by far the best overall resource I have found for guiding one to a healthy life. And I think the reason I like it so much is that it does the best job of covering the abstract science, as well giving ideas about how that science might influence one’s day to day choices.
	- By increasing the focus on the three areas outlined above, I think MDA could really build on its greatest strength and be even more valuable to its readership.

	- Read more: [http://www.marksdailyapple.com/dear-readers-what-do-you-want/#ixzz1vhZ6VfiX](http://www.marksdailyapple.com/dear-readers-what-do-you-want/#ixzz1vhZ6VfiX)
	- Bold & Determined's expansion suggestions
	- Making Money Hurts People’s Feelings (but so what)
	- APRIL 20, 2015 BY VICTOR PRIDE545 COMMENTS
	- From the desk of Victor PrideSubj: Money + Feelings = Crybabies————
	- I recently met with a local realtor who was interested in selling his realty business.
	- He wanted 80k for the business. Fine.
	- While I’m not willing to go out and show houses to people, I’m perfectly interested in looking at the business opportunity.
	- If the numbers work I am perfectly willing to buy any business.
	- The problem with the realty business?
	- The problem is that the realtor is the business.
	- Without him doing the work there is no revenue. Without revenue there is no business.
	- You couldn’t buy his business today and have money coming in tomorrow. You’d have to go out and find new business to make money.
	- If someone were to purchase his business they would essentially be starting out as a brand new realtor and they’d be in the hole 80k.
	- Then they’d have to go out and cold call and knock on doors to start digging themselves out of that $80,000 hole.
	- Freelancer vs Business Owner
	- Without revenue there is no business and the realty business wasn’t a real business.
	- The owner was essentially a freelancer, getting paid when he got clients to sign and not getting paid when no one signed.
	- He should have taken steps to outsource the work to employees. He should have had systems in place to make money when he was not around.
	- Instead, he worked as a sole proprietor for ten years. He made enough money to buy a house in Australia, but he didn’t take steps to make his realty freelancing a real business.
	- Now he’s in the position of having worked on this gig for ten years and no one will buy it because there’s nothing to buy.
	- Businesses should be scalable and saleable
	- His realty business was nothing more than some phone numbers and connections, but phone numbers and introductions aren’t worth $80,000.
	- Only a system that can make money for anyone is worth 80k.
	- So the realtor is stuck with his non-business.
	- Contrast that realty non-business with the business of B&D
	- If one were to purchase B&D today (not for sale) he would have immediate income tomorrow and next week and next month.
	- Money always come in, no matter what else happens, because I put systems in place to make sure money comes in.
	- Even if I died tomorrow, B&D would still make money. The systems are already in place. The work is already done.
	- Example: I recently broke my hand in two places.
	- It was broken so bad that I had to have surgery to put pins in my hand. After the surgery I had to wear a cast for four weeks.
	- In total, my hand was useless for eight weeks.
	- I couldn’t go to the gym, I couldn’t type, I couldn’t ride my motorbike, I couldn’t do much of anything that I enjoy doing.
	- Since I didn’t write I must have lost income right?
	- Wrong.
	- The two months I was out of commission were the fiscally best months B&D has ever had.
	- Why is that? How did the business make money when I didn’t appear to do any work?
	- The magic of residual income
	- I don’t like the term passive income – I never made money passively – the term residual income fits much better.
	- You do the work once, then you get paid for it residually – as long as the work is good.
	- Like a songwriter who writes a hit song or an author who writes a hit book.
	- They do the actual work one time, then they get paid for it for however long people want to buy it.
	- There’s nothing passive about creating
	- The songwriter and book author didn’t make that money passively, they actively wrote the song or book, then they got paid residually.
	- And that’s how I got paid while I didn’t appear to work.
	- Speaking of not appearing to work…
	- The myth of struggle
	- A lot of people have asked me about my struggles to make a nothing into a something.
	- I don’t particularly enjoy reading or writing about struggle, so I don’t.
	- The reality is that I haven’t struggled at all. For me, in fact, it was easy to make Bold and Determined a success.
	- That’s what I keep saying over and over and over again…
	- It’s not hard to do what I do!
	- It’s much harder to work some job you hate for a paycheck that leaves you scraping by.
	- My life is phenomenally easy compared to any Average Joe working his average job.
	- I often romanticize the fact that I didn’t make money for over a year.
	- It’s true, I didn’t make a dime for over a year. But let me tell you two things…
	  collapsed:: true
		- That year wasn’t hard at all. It was one of the best years of my life.
		- I didn’t try to make money for a year. I knew it would come eventually so I just concentrated on building an audience. A year later, when I tried to make money, I did make money.I know it will hurt some feelings to hear that it was super-easy for me, but I’ve never been bothered by hurting feelings.
	- It’s much worse to hear successful people lie about “the struggle”
	- When you hear the lies about struggling your mind is tricked into thinking that since you’re struggling you’re on the right path.
	- Wrong.
	- When you’re on the right path it will be easy. It’s only when you’re on the wrong path that it’s hard.
	- Whatever you were meant do, IF you were mean to do anything, will be easy. That’s the cold, hard reality.
	- If you live a pathetic life you don’t have the right to complain about struggle because you and you alone have the ability to change your life.
	- If you don’t change it, that’s your fault. If you’re struggling it’s your own fault.
	- You, you, you, you, you, you, you, you, you, you, you.
	- Not me, not him, not her, not that corporation, not the government…
	- YOU!
	- If your life is a struggle, you are the problem.
	- It might just be that you aren’t smart enough or talented enough to make it
	- ..or it might be that you aren’t trying.
	- Whichever it is, you get what you deserve.
	- It’s very easy for me to make money, it’s not hard at all.
	- People HATE to hear that but I don’t care.
	- Haters can hate all they want but if life is a struggle, it’s your duty to fix it.
	- Most people won’t fix it and I don’t care in the slightest.
	- If you don’t want to fix it I won’t offer a helping hand.
	- It’s an inevitablity of success that the lower classes first worship you then turn on you.
	- Which brings me to…
	- Making Money Hurts People’s Feelings
	- YouTube has become extremely successful by giving a voice to the voiceless.
	- The comments section on youtube gives anyone who has internet access a chance to voice their opinion.
	- That sounds great in theory but the reality is that most people are small, petty and silly and we don’t need to hear their silly opinions.
	- YouTube commenters are probably a perfect representation of normal people and I see two trends among YouTube commenters/normal people.
	- The first trend is this…
	  collapsed:: true
		- Anyone who makes money is greedy and a piece of shit.
		- Anyone who is poor should be given money.Huh?
	- That’s right. Making money is evil and you should give poor people money (even though it’s evil).
	- The 2nd trend I see among YouTube commenters is this…
	- They have poor english skills, poor writing abilities, and poor comprehension.
	- The average comment length is one to three sentences but they’re often impossible to read.
	- People who can’t even take the time to use capitalization and punctuation certainly don’t have the attention span (or the will) to master a money-making skill.
	- Commenters with readable english often have different ideas about money…
	- But listen boys, here’s the facts of life…
	- If poor people wanted to make money they would.
	- Poor and stupid can be used interchangeably.
	- But even stupid people can make money.
	- To find those YouTube comments I typed “Floyd Mayweather Money” in the search bar and clicked on two videos.
	- Floyd Mayweather Jr. is a rich and famous boxer who inspires jealously, hatred and envy in ordinary people. It only took a few moments to find some jealous comments on his YouTube videos.
	- The funny thing?
	- Floyd Mayweather can barely read but he’s rich and famous.
	- If someone who can’t even read can make money, what does that mean for smart people who are broke…
	- Anyone who wants to make money, makes money
	- If making money is a priority to you, you will make it.
	- If you don’t make money it’s because you don’t want to.
	- In reality, losers don’t want to make money, they want to be given money.
	- I know that hurts to hear, but that’s what tough love is.
	- You can hear lies to feel better, or you can hear the truth to get better.
	- Only a loser is mad at the truth of the world.
	- A winner can hear the truth, accept the truth, internalize the truth, and then they can become something.
	- It is what it is – so make it work for you
	- I keep telling you, I’m not so special that only I can make a living being me.
	- You can do it too, if you want to.
	- I know people will tell you it’s impossible, but what are you looking for from them?
	- Permission?
	- You have my express permission to not require permission. OK?
	- But if you actually need permission you don’t belong in the big leagues and you don’t deserve success and freedom.
	- So stop pretending.
	- Until next time.
	- Your man,
	- -Victor Pride
	- BONUS – A Chance to Make $500
	- Now here is your chance to make some money and hurt some people’s feelings.
	- You can make up to $500 for thirty seconds of work.
	- Here’s how…
	- All you have to do is give the best business tip/idea to Bold and Determined.
	- The idea should be specific to Bold and Determined.
	- You give me a great idea, you get $500 in return. It’s as simple as that.
	- Leave a comment below with your idea to make B&D, BADNET, BADWEAR, 30DOD or BOAS better, smoother and more profitable.

	  collapsed:: true

		- You must promise to keep the money and not give it to charity if you win.
		- You must leave your idea as a comment below – do not send your idea via email.Ideas that will not win:
		- You should write a new book.
		- You should make a video trailer for Body of a Spartan.
		- You should write more.
		- You should start a forum.
		- You should offer consulting.
		- You should do a regular podcast/video series.Those ideas will not win because, duh, I already know them. But more than that, they won’t win because they rely on me doing the work (like the realtor).
	- B&D is already a well-oiled machine, but it can be better and go faster. Only a small change needs to be made.
	- Right now, this very moment, 50 things could be changed on B&D to make a profit and to make the work more enjoyable to read.
	- Your job, should you wish to make some money, is to find those things and point them out to me.
	- Oh, by the way, three people will win.
	  collapsed:: true

		- 2nd prize wins $250
		- 3rd prize wins a SPARTAN t-shirt.The winners will be chosen and announced on Monday, April 27.

	- There are no limits to where you live, your age, your race, your nothing. Best idea(s) will win money.
	- I’m taking a gamble and betting that the majority readers of B&D are smart fellows.
	- So who’s it gonna be?

		- Matt says
	- April 22, 2015 at 6:07 am
	- Let me take that one step further: Adrafinil
	- In a nutshell, adrafinil metabolizes in modafinil after you swallow it. The effect is exactly the same, it just takes an extra few minutes to achieve.
	- However, legally speaking:
	- – Modafinil is currently classified as a Schedule IV controlled substance under United States federal law; it is illegal to import by anyone other than a DEA-registered importer without a prescription.
	- – In the United States, adrafinil is currently unregulated. Unlike modafinil, it is not a controlled substance even though the medical effects are essentially the same.
	- I’ve bought modafinil from India before, but if B&D is looking for a completely legal alternative then Adrafinil might be the way to go

		- StS says
	- April 21, 2015 at 3:44 pm
	- “You can hear lies to feel better, or you can hear the truth to get better. Only a loser is mad at the truth of the world.” That’s the essence of B&D and similar sites condensed in 2 sentences – Simplicity is Magic
	- People write here about B&D in other languages…for all GERMAN speakers, I kindly invite you to visit my site hirnherzundmuskel.com. Please visit, leave comments, provide feedback and if you like the page, subscribe to the newsletter.
	- And for you, Victor: What about a professionally conceptualized and designed “market survey” concerning business, weights & nutrition and how it relates to B&D?Working in pharma marketing, where you adress doctors by means which are different from “normal customers”, I can tell you that surveys offer some great benefits:1) You get a lot of information from the market segment, which is most relevant to you, by asking very specific questions. And you can use this info in turn for new business ideas.2) People remember you and your messages much more when the info exchange is bi-directional: When people only read, they quickly forget. When the read, think and write about things, the info sticks in their head much longer. (E.g. when we ask doctors to rank the specified advantages of a given product, we know firstly, which messages to use for communication and secondly, and much more important, just by thinking about the various advantages of a product, the doctors internalize them)3) It’s a very good trap for newcomers. People taking the survey will hang around as long as the survey takes and this also increases the possibility of them staying longer after finishing the survey, reading your other content.4) People LOVE to learn stuff about themselves, so a combination of gathering information about them and telling them somethin about themselves in return is a satisfying experience.

		- Alex says
	- April 20, 2015 at 9:14 pm
	- Victor,
	- You’ve got a great network of products, you create trust and sell with your authenticity, and you seem to have the backend system that automates everything perfectly.
	- I could give you more ideas for things to sell, but I’d like to share more of a technical tip and something I’ve recently just implemented to my own eCommerce site that could help you sell what you already have a little more:
	- Have your web guys switch B&D, BOAS, BADNET, 30DOD and whatever else you do to HTTPS
	- (I notice your checkout pages are already HTTPS, which is great, but I think you could benefit from having it sitewide too)
	- In short, it’s a security thing:
	- “[…] when a user enters data into a form on your site in order to subscribe to updates or purchase a product, a secure site protects that user’s personal information and ensures that the user communicates with the authorized owner of the site.…but I think the true benefits of this come from how it better helps people perceive your website at first glance:
	- Most sites aren’t HTTPS, so it’s a professional way to stand out further from amateurs.When I go to BADNET in my browser, I would clearly trust you to build me a website when I see this in my URL bar. Mobile users see a “lock” icon.Ever try visiting a site over coffee shop or shaky wifi? This should help you avoid this kind of nasty error message.
	- And as a bonus: Google even says this helps improve search rankings.
	- Like I said, I just implemented SSL/HTTPS to my own site so I have no “data” for you on how it could actually improve your sales. But as far as setting up a professional website and creating a more secure eCommerce environment, having an SSL certificate / HTTPS are absolute musts.

	- BADnet has a target demographic – young men, generally those in the audience known as the manosphere today. This demographic determines the size and scope of audience, and all that entails. 	- The suggestion is a multi-branding approach of existing content, with each brand universe targeting a different demographic. This could lead to a franchising of the business – say a BADnet rebranding targeting professional women in business as the base foundation, with vetted female writers providing further content towards that demographic.
	- This turns BADnet into an institution, and is among the most successful business approaches online for content publishers. It scales in multiple dimensions.

		- Riz says
	- April 20, 2015 at 10:32 pm
	- Want even more traffic, and thus more cash? Invest in education and consulting on SEO.Here’s three reasons why:
	- 1) Content is king – but SEO is the war council. You’re missing out on a tremendous level of opportunity by not at least checking in on ultra-optimization tactics. Case in point – tomorrow Google officially hates on non-mobile friendly sites. 60% of all search traffic is now coming from mobile. For anyone here, you’ll disappear from mobile search if you don’t pass the mobile friendly test on any site:https://www.google.com/webmasters/tools/mobile-friendly/
	- 2) URL structures – this post URL is “http://boldanddetermined.com/making-money-hurts-peoples-feelings/” – you could have done better. Bold and Determined is considered a great brand in the eyes of Google – I know because I can see extended metrics. If this post URL was something such as “http://boldanddetermined.com/business-strategies-for-residual-income” your chances for random traffic are much higher, because that is something people might actually search. You can make post and page titles whatever you want – not the same as the raw URL.
	- 3) Cheat – let’s face it. People game the system, in both black hat and grey hat ways. You can automate social signals for instance which Google absolutely loves. Just one plugin can increase your traffic by 50% because you can pay for Twitter, Delicious, Diigo, etc. posts. Social is the key moving forward. If your content isn’t on the sites with the most traffic in the world, why would Google give you any weight?
	- I paid a tremendous amount of money for tutoring from men that make 2 million per year by harnessing the power of search. One of these men took the time to study the Google patents. With this knowledge, the world belongs to him.
	- And it can be yours too.

	- I have completed a quick run through and come up with about 12 ideas, but i will just pick the three that stood out. I am including a risk category as well.
	- 6. Affiliate links/ some kind of satellite about getting set up in east Asia. More specifically Thailand or Vietnam.I would wager there are a number of people looking for that kind of content but not knowing who would rip them off or not. You leverage your connections, and make a nice cut in the middle.Risk: Medium to Low. You’re only recommending people, but bad people recommended with also put a dent into your reputation.
	- 8. BADwear range for wives or girlfriends of BADreaders. This is a no brainer, Guys like seeing their princesses dress up in cute vests/ tees/cutoffs. Plus you get to have cute chicks (be selective) wearing your clothing range, that’s promotional merchandise right there.
	- Risk: Low to None. As i said, its a no brainer.
	- 11. BADstarter. Essentially kickstarter or indiegogo for Bold and determined readers. People come up with an idea, put it up. Men vote with their wallets, and if it gets the necessary funding and traction, they get a business out of it. You take a 10-20% cut for hosting their gig on your site. Make it better than indiegogo which allows people to keep the money even if they fail their target. You want to discourage the scam artists and encourage the idea men who don’t have enough capital to raise on their own.
	- Risk: Medium to High. You have to be careful about scam artists, using your site as an opportunity to make fast money and cut and run. Unfortunately their reputation would translate back to the site as well. Good people, Good Rep, Good site = more profits. And vice versa.

		- Jack says
	- April 20, 2015 at 11:19 pm
	- Hey Victor,
	- I notice that you are using YouTube for your videos. Something better than YouTube is to use your own video service. What I recommended for Mike, was to use Wistia.
	- I did a quick search for one of your YouTube videos “A Quick Tip to Beat Procrastination Forever” and it ranks #1 in google. However, all the other results are no-name websites. In addition, there isn’t any info linking back to “B&D” once the person finds your video page.
	- When I type in “Success Rebel” into google, your YouTube video comes up first as #1.
	- If you were to use Wistia, you would avoid this problem. Your blog should be #1 for this and not the YouTube page which doesn’t link back to your blog.
	- You may think that simply embeding YouTube videos into yoru blog post will solve this problem, but what your actually doing is giving the YouTube video page credit.
	- Wisita videos also look more professional and you can customize it, un-like the crap YouTube player.
	- You can also capture e-mails after the video is done playing. Lot’s of people use it for their sales pages, yours could benefit by using it.
	- Finally, I noticed your site doesn’t use Cloudflare (free), I would look into using it, to filter out spam, and to secure your site more.

		- John Shea says
	- April 20, 2015 at 11:19 pm
	- Hi Victor,
	- Great post here, I enjoyed the comparison of your blog and website properties vs. an entirely different business model. Being an entrepreneur allowed you to continue to drive revenue even while you were out of commission for a couple of months, awesome stuff!
	- I really enjoyed the 30 days of discipline program. As you know I even made a podcast and an entire blog dedicated to the program. I laugh a little inside because if I put the effort into a program like you did instead of blogging about yours I probably could have made a pretty kickass program myself and made more money that way!
	- Well anyway here is my idea:
	- I would come up with another program similar to this, the difference being that it would focus more on sacrifice vs. being mostly disciplined. Call it the “30 days of sacrifice” or maybe 60 / 90 days instead. The tagline could include something along the lines of achieving more success and becoming an entrepreneur.
	- Some ideas:-Make the program geared towards specific goals for people to start achieving success with a blog, easily tied into BADNET. Your new eBook covers a lot of this but it’s a long read with tons of ideas to take action with. I find that content like that is harder to take action when you don’t have a plan in place. I’d want it laid out with action steps of what to do each day or week, month etc.
	- -Include sacrifices like video games and alcohol, partying etc. I added these to the 30 days of discipline and I think if I didn’t I would have failed miserably.
	- -Think of other things people do on a daily basis that is basically a waste of time, things that don’t lead people to success. Another example of sacrifice would be no TV during the program, I know that’s huge for a lot of people.
	- -During the program they must follow a specific set of steps to improve their life while sacrificing those things that hinder them and hold them back from success. Maybe it’s as simple as consuming lots of water, taking a multi-vitamin, going for a brisk 15 minute jog daily etc.
	- -Involve eating healthy and other home gym workouts in some way shape or form, it does not need to be extreme like body of a spartan but perhaps ways they can integrate more of an even balance for long term results. Mix it up more vs the 3 exercises x100.
	- -Make a big part of the program dedicated to focus, in 30 days you just mentioned setting goals and it was very broad with no real ideas. Give people an idea of what they can work towards, even if they don’t make X amount of dollars after X days of a program I can see a lot of people having an overall better sense of life and their future if they stay on this path of doing positive things daily to strive towards success, convert people into full blown entrepreneurs.
	- -Create a system, or website where people can communicate about progress (Forum of sorts), sacrifices they have made and maybe a tracker that is online (not a simple PDF check list) but a full blown community/tracking system to guide people through progress. People can watch each others progress, encourage others etc.
	- -Involve the community more, maybe people can invent their own ideas for the program, make it a pole or vote. Hit up your current email list of 30 days of discipline buyers and get a vote for what should be part of the program.
	- -Feature members who achieve success with the program on B&D (Or new community site), award recognition, prizes, etc.
	- -Ditch e-Junkie, I felt like a prick emailing you about commission payouts because I had no clue how your payouts worked (Thank you for the payment finally!). Switch to something like Jvzoo, offer the 75% or whatever and just let that platform handle it all with Paypal instantly. I’ve done over 20k in sales with the platform and wouldn’t touch another system, it’s ease of use and ability to work with systems like Wishlist member, GetResponse etc. make it a no brainer. You could also offer prizes to your best affiliates encouraging program growth overall.
	- Well hopefully you like my idea, I have built several membership sites and would be glad to help where needed if you decide to take me up on my idea.
	- I mention focus because I started up an SEO business for insurance companies and it’s been picking up for me, got a partner on board and everything. I’d love to build a blog like B&D on the side but if I jump into all these different things I won’t get anywhere, I think this program should really help people understand that. I have spent years trying to do tons of different things, most projects only work when I really sink tons of time into them, nothing will be an overnight success story and that’s why I’m sticking with this business I got going. Thanks
	- -John

		- tj says
	- April 20, 2015 at 11:19 pm
	- Great article ( as usual ) but here’s a small point. I used to make these kinds of assumptions/generalizations about stranger’s comments: “People who can’t even take the time to use capitalization and punctuation certainly don’t have the attention span (or the will) to master a money-making skill.” Then one day I met a Kung Fu master who frequently wrote without capitalization or punctuation. I have no idea why he chose to write that way ( and I still dont ), but he certainly had plenty of will and a rock solid attention span. While I absolutely see what you’re getting at, the truth is we never know who someone is on the internet, what their background is or what skills they may possess. Not everyone does things the same way ( or follows the writing ‘rules’ ) and to make an leap or an assumption about someone’s character based on their writing style can backfire on us. Thanks again for sharing your experiences with us.

	- If there are a lot people are interested in living like you, then there are also a lot of people interested in living where you live as well. Depending on where you are living now, you probably have convenient access to the local businesses, real estate brokers, services etc.. You also have a pretty big mailing list of an audience that more than likely would find value in the site.
	- It’s scalable, saleable and can be a source of residual income. A site like this could easily be built on wordpress as well.

What ways are there to make money? Where do you go shopping? Ever had the shits after eating something from the street vendors? How much is a taxi ride? What banks are there?…. and all those little things most travel bloggers seem to completely forget about.

		- Michael says
	- April 20, 2015 at 11:25 pm
	- Hire a like-minded editor to read your posts, and rewrite them and the views you are trying to express in a different way. Not to say that your writing style or mode of expression is bad (I enjoy it), but you could reach a broader range of people. The same idea can be expressed in many different ways. Some people can’t interpret ideas correctly if they are expressed in a certain way.
	- Having someone who understands your mindset and is on the same page as you, but who expresses themselves about those ideas in a different way than you do could be beneficial to expanding your audience (while still maintaining the integrity of the readership).
	- You’d still provide the ideas and write the articles, but the editor would come up with new ways of expressing or clarifying those core ideas. And re-reading your own ideas from a different perspective might give you new incites that you could further synthesize into your posts. It would help your creativity too.

		- Louis says
	- April 20, 2015 at 11:39 pm
	- Great post, great blog. Great marketing ploy as well. This is my first comment here since I don’t usually do the commenting thing, but your bonus was too tasty not to bite.
	- So here goes.
	- From what I know you’ve got a couple of high quality products that all have a common denominator, namely they fit right into the Bold & Determined lifestyle/mindset.
	- On the other hand, these products lack visibility and a cohesive marketing story. On top of that, you are not using a leadmagnet to entice newcomers to subscribe to your website.
	- Yes, your blog is seriously good there’s a good chance people will subscribe eventually. However there’s no point in ignoring proven marketing tactics that improve your conversion rate drasticly. There just isn’t. Psychology works for everyone as you know well enough.
	- There is a great streamlining opportunity here.
	- I would suggest a couple of changes in your website structure that will have significant impact on your subscribers and sales conversion.
	- 1. Create an About page where most of your current “New? Start Here” content will be transferred to. You could even go into even more depth about B&D and your personal story which creates more rapport with your readers. Young men love inspiration. You’ve got the authenticity and life experience to provide them with it.
	- 2. That said, the first step is mainly to make way for the second. I would design a new “Start Here” page where you create a landing page that explains what B&D is and why it is a must-have resource for the up and coming wolves. Pitch your entire brand, including yourself as the leader-by-example using proper copy. However there is no need for excruciating detail as this is covered in the About page which you can refer to. Keep it simple and powerful. Also keep in mind the visual aspect of your text. Internet users love headlines and scannability. I have to say the scannability of your current “Start Here” page is a mess.
	- 3. At the bottom and(/or) in the middle of the page, add a 2 step opt-in (check out LeadBoxes: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=AHYqoI9uX-k) where you offer them an exclusive post (that you will obviously launch to your old subscribers as well) named something along the lines of “The Ultimate Guide to walking the Bold & Determined path”. This is the gift that they will receive upon subscribing.
	- Creating this post will take some effort, but it would basicly be an in-depth guide to utilizing your own products and top posts to make the most out of what you and your brand has to offer, especially if you are just discovering the website. Break it down so that people can read this post and have a lasting framework to dig deeper into your content and products.
	- Not only is this a great way to get more subscribers, you can also pitch your products properly and give them the attention they deserve. For instance, I currently have a relatively hard time finding out BADwear even exists. Make it easier and more appealing this way. (Of course general tweaks can never hurt either.)
	- You could even break this ‘post’ up in several mails to prevent your readers from being bombared with too much information all at once. Breaking things up will also allow you to let your readers focus on your products at exactly the right time, without feeling overwhelmed.
	- This is the core of how I would improve and streamline your current content and brand. There are several other small tweaks (such as custom Opt-in boxes specified for certain posts, 2 step Opt-ins in general, a more straightforward approach to pitching and offering products, etc) which are going to help your business, but I think the idea above is the one that will have the largest direct impact and is worth implementing first.
	- Well, that’s it from me.
	- Peace,Louis

		- Lenwood says
	- April 21, 2015 at 12:31 am
	- I didn’t read the other comments, so this may have already been suggested (and it is a very obvious idea), but:You should allow featured/sponsored content. Obviously, it would have to be a quality article that fits into your own vision, and you would need to guarantee yourself full editorial control so that you don’t water down your content with garbage, but this would give hungry guys a chance to advertise their own stuff on your site, and you could collect a cool $1500-2000 once a month for allowing a guest post. I’m sure there are guys who would pay at least that for one 1,000 word post on your platform. Charge $2 per word so that it reinforces the need for brevity and to cut out the bullshit.
	- You’ve done the hard work of building the platform. Allow at most one per month so that it remains a valuable commodity. Your only labor would be reading a post and editing it — oh, and collecting someone’s billing information.

		- Tyson Wolf says
	- April 21, 2015 at 12:48 am
	- This post in and of itself was the best idea.
	- Utilizing your entire B&D audience of aspiring entrepreneurs as an idea tank for less than $800. There’s a lot of good ideas in here too, which supports what you were saying about how many people are going to have the smarts to be successful but aren’t trying hard enough.
	- The real value behind this blog, for me at least, has been to watch the way in which it has evolved; in how your business model has sort of adapted over the past year or two, in terms of the type of value you are providing. I know that’s been really insightful for me to take note of and remember the importance of building a business that can flex and adapt over time to allow for expansion in different directions.
	- Anyway, seeing where your business has come from and where it seems to be going, I’d say that now would be a good time for you begin distancing yourself from the equation. While your business generates money regardless of whether or not you are around, a large part of it is content driven, and being the sole author and artist of B&D, it can’t “expand” (in content) without you. What I would likely do if I were in your shoes is this:
	- (a) Create an exclusive Bold&Determined “Club” / collective. Many of your readers are now aspiring to follow in your path, but are making the mistake of trying to “copycat” from you, as well as advertising their sites to one another, as opposed to acquiring new readers from the 7 billion other people in the world who don’t currently subscribe to any blogs. This BADCLUB/BADPACK/etc. would grant select individuals membership to a private group (hidden Facebook group, private forum, etc.) where they could network with one another, promote each others sites, bounce ideas and suggestions off of each other, etc. Honest feedback from one another would help them to create their own unique voice and business, rather than having a bunch of B&D “same same but differents.” You could offer it as an optional, but recommended component of BADNET and charge a monthly or annual subscription fee, which would benefit subscribers in the long run, but serve as straight passive income for yourself. Furthermore, tying your readers together in this way would help them to succeed in their entrepreneurial goals, lending further positive testimony to the effectiveness of BADNET. People would subscribe to this, and it would be easy, straight profit for you, month after month.
	- (b) In addition to/rather than this, you could create a satellite site of guest posts only. This should be a different site, so that there is no risk of losing your audience because of it. You could compile a list of all BADNET-affiliated sites, read the posts over lunch, and choose one per week to feature on the new blog. Most of your readers will likely immediately hop onto and subscribe to that blog as well, so you wouldn’t have to go through all the legwork of building another list from scratch. It would be up to your discretion if anyone’s posts are eligible for being included on this site, or if you only chose from those in the BADCLUB previously mentioned. Traffic and publicity for BADNET customers / BADCLUB subscribers; lack of pressure to generate content on your own. To take advantage of the current viral nature of social media, you could promote the concept of sharing one another’s work from this blog on Facebook/Twitter etc., because the end result would be massive influxes of new readers who had never previously heard of B&D or any of the blogs/businesses by guys on here.
	- Less work for Victor Pride, more money for everyone.

		- Matt says
	- April 21, 2015 at 2:17 am
	- Not really a long thought out idea to improve revenues, but a useful suggestion to a problem you may not know you have that could be ruining your user experience for the last week or more.
	- I just discovered your blog two weeks ago for the first time. Since, I’ve been devouring different sections each day in my spare time in the evenings. Your site has been throwing db errors intermittently and doesn’t load for a few minutes at a time every so often. I’m not on the site very much, but if it’s happened to me multiple times, it might be much more frequent which could be affecting traffic and sales.
	- screenshot – http://prntscr.com/6w5m20
	- I’d imagine the server is getting hit pretty hard at times, or the database isn’t optimized, cached, and missing indexes if db is large. I’m not sure if you’re aware that Hostgator was bought by EIG, but normally hosting companies decline after that acquisition. (no idea if that’s the issue or not, I just saw you mentioned you’re on an HG dedi in another post somewhere. I ditched a lot of my hostgator accounts after they went to shit in the past)
	- Steps to fix this:
	- 1) Open a support ticket and ask host to optimize db and user account.
	- 2) Fix wordpress cache – Fastest cache is currently 1.2 second load time on Genesis framework? Should be faster with a dedi
	- 3) Add a cdn – cloudflare or cloudfront for extended uptime and load times around the world
	- 4) Setup an uptime monitor with https://uptimerobot.com or http://pingdom.com to be aware if the problem persists and take the next preventative steps (don’t use a service that pings the server every few seconds, that’ll just add to the problem and waste resources. You just need an ongoing overview of what’s happening, and some sort of third party notification when the site becomes unavailable.)
	- Pitfalls: host might say you have too much traffic and you need to upgrade yada yada. (they’re notorious for this, instead of fixing the problem… throwing resources at it only works for so long, especially if you truly are already on a dedicated server. It would be the equivalent of a kid saying nothing in his life changed after completing 30DOD… but the bitch only woke up at 5am once.) They might be right about upgrading, but I doubt it… couldn’t say for sure without knowing server specs and daily connections.
	- You could switch to “wordpress hosting” like synthesis, wp engine, or pagely that everyone says is “the fastest” if Hostgator can’t help you. Personally I think most of those are horse shit in the long run.
	- If you do end up needing to switch hosting companies, check out http://unixy.net and get a server with Varnish… it’ll cache everything at the server level. Plus Joe the owner is amazeballs when it comes to complex hosting solutions and crippling servers. He’s helped me out of a bind when my storm servers at liquidweb went to shit on more than one occasion.
	- Hope that helps!
	- Great blog Victor, enjoying it so far!

		- Quinn says
	- April 21, 2015 at 5:47 am
	- IDEA #1
	- Work Required: Very MinimalPotential Payoff: More than enough to pay for your steaks
	- Had this idea a couple weeks ago. I saw your new ad on thefastlaneforum, which was a great move, but there’s a couple things you can do to get more readers and more sales from this advertisement.
	- Right now, people click on the ad and come to your homepage. This is okay, and visitors still could turn into loyal readers because your site is so great, but there’s a couple ways you could increase the chances of a visitor turning into loyal, long-term readers who will eventually purchase your products and make you more money.
	- The demographic/interest fit with the fastlane forum is perfect for your blog (I found your site through the forum 2-3 years ago).
	- First, you could send them to the “New? Start here” page so they understand exactly who you are and what your site is about, and you could point them directly to your most popular pages from there. This is better than sending them to the home page because you’re now sending visitors to the information and pages they will connect with and like most, as opposed to letting them find it themselves from the home page.
	- Second option is you could send them directly to 1 single post that would be very popular with them. The first post I saw when I was referred from the fastlane forum 2-3 years ago was “The 21 rules of the rich”. I was sent to a specific page and eventually became a loyal reader. If I just stumbled upon your home page, I’m not so sure I would read as much or stuck around.
	- Third option is you could send the visitors directly to your 30DOD page and sell them that. I know personally from seeing the large number of clueless posts on there that many of them need 30DOD. I know it’s not something you do with your products, but you could even offer a special discount for the fastlane forum (10-15% off?) from this ad.
	- And it goes without saying that you’d need to adjust your creative to be more specific for the page you’re sending them to. Either way, the demographic and interest is definitely a great fit with this ad, but I believe you could get more loyal readers and more sales from the forum by being more specific.
	- IDEA #2 (My favorite)
	- BAD Academy™ (a permanent coworking space in Saigon)
	- There’s several coworking spaces in places like Saigon, but none like this. Many of your readers would love to move to Vietnam and do nothing but work on a business of their own 24/7.
	- So here’s the idea.
	- Either use your own place, or rent/buy another place to rent out to aspiring BAD Academy™ students for a monthly fee as a permanent coworking space – somewhere they can eat, sleep, and work on their businesses 24/7, and do it with a group of other BAD Academy™ students who want nothing but the same things as them: freedom, money, building a BADass body at the gym every morning, and a business of their own.
	- Imagine this.
	- Imagine a group of 5-10 people (you could take applications or something and pick only the real winners) who are all living 30DOD, taking Modafinil, and killing it every motherfucking day.
	- All you would have to do is organize the whole thing, collect the monthly payments, and maybe stop in once every week or two or whenever you wanted to help some of them out if you wanted. BAD Academy™ and Professor Pride with whole Army of BAD soldiers working together to get shit done.
	- If anyone is slacking, he either gets it together or he’s out. Gone. Doesn’t matter if it’s a blog, an ecommerce business or what. As long as he’s working his ass off, and getting shit done.
	- You would give the students a productive environment like no other on Earth, and build a whole new network yourself. This would be truly taking your empire to the next level.
	- THE NUMBERS
	- Say you rented out a separate place to use: I’m not too sure of prices there but say you got a 6 bedroom place around $2000 a month.
	- You rented it with 2 people/ bedroom at $1000 per month. That would be 12 people and $10,000 per month profit.
	- You could always go with a bigger place or more people and make more money, or you could get creative and be a “Shark” like Mark Cuban, offering a lower rent in exchange for equity in the businesses started there. You would eventually have a little bit of equity in a large number of businesses and be bigger than you ever imagined.
	- Or you could take a certain % of their profits for the first year or two of the business. (See appacademy.io)
	- The profit potential for this could be huge, but it would be about so much more than the money. You would make your empire bigger than ever and leave a huge, lasting impact on the world.
	- Go big or go home.
	- I’ve got another idea too to help your business but I’ll stop here for now, haha. I could come up with ideas to help Bold and Determined all day long. I just love this shit.

	- Hi Victor,
	- I would suggest you to start e-Magazine. Why? Let me give you the detailed analysis. For explanation purposes, let me call this Bold and Determined as Business and its viewers / Subscribers as Customers.
	- Creating a premium content (As suggested by Vernon – other fellow commenter) and charging for it specially makes this blog seem not friendly to new Customers. Because, think about it, We know the worth of your content, but not new viewers. (To explain this simply, new viewers don’t buy your books immediately after knowing about your blog. They will later on, after reading your content and realizing that what you’re preaching is THE reality. Then only they are convinced to buy your Books.)
	- And it not usual for a blog to make it a paid subscription blog, whether it may be written blog or a Video blog in YouTube. These are items expected to be free.But, by launching a magazine you could do the same. I.e. Write exclusive content and get paid for it. You can charge for it and people won’t perceive it as the same thing. Because, its another product of BAD World. Just like other things people already pay for I.e. your eBooks, BADWEAR and BADNET.
	- And by launching the magazine you will have different opportunities like publishing Ads for your own products. You can publish new designs arrived at BADWEAR. You can promote this magazine by providing discounts for your other products to magazine subscribers only. Thus promoting the sales of both the magazine and your other products. And you can sell your magazine in many places like iTunes App Store Newsstand and Google Play Newsstand. You can consider selling your books in Google PlayStore and iTunes Appstore. As you said you are making an App, you can add this as a feature of Paid Version of the App. (Yeah, create app with free and paid versions if you want to.) Take your pick, there are many opportunities.( For ads, you can provide hyperlinks just like you do in this blog, for your eBooks, other posts etc. Because, its an eMagazine. If you are thinking about an opening for advertising outside content, you could do that too. As you don’t do that in this blog.)
	- As for the content of the blog, you can write about suggestions for aspiring bloggers. What do you do when you have a writers block, write about your journey to achieving this stage instead of doing it in podcasts. Why? Because people want to hear your story. Here I just gave my suggestions, you pick your content. You’re the content writer.
	- Thats pretty much it about magazine.

	- You know, I’ve been a long time reader of your site and I know you’re probably going to pass on most of these BS ideas because well they’re just not profitable enough. Give me a second, and I might just change your life.
	- Once upon a time I saw this guy Armando Montelongo who hosts real estate conventions to people who want to make money in real estate. These people are your everyday run of the mill people going to this mans “idea seminar,” because they believe they will get rich. Tons and tons of people go to his conventions and buy his product, but why? Because word of mouth travels, and if you can get people to tell their friends about a “great way to make money,” they’ll follow like sheep because they will trust their friends before some shady guy on an infomercial.Just look at companies like “Herbalife,” they’re MLM’s and there most definitely frauds but yet they hear from there friends they can make money and they follow like sheep. Because they trust them, and without trust there is no sale.
	- Remember, “A fool is born every minute.”
	- The most hilarious part of this story is the fact that his verified income statements show he’s only made 180K doing what he preaches will make people rich overnight. Mr.Montelongo actually made closer to $200 million off of his infomercials & conventions etc. Selling informational products that are ineffective at best. He’s not good at real estate, but he’s smart at business and that’s why he’s got millions.
	- Here’s the link to him & his story.(http://www.forbes.com/sites/abrambrown/2013/06/26/meet-armando-montelongo-the-home-flipping-huckster-wholl-make-50m-this-year/)

	- Same pattern, same result.
	- Anyway, It’s time to focus.
	- So here’s the plan to get rich…
	- Are you ready?
	- Step 1): formulate “get rich quick scheme,” doesn’t matter if you’re good or not. Can be anything like stocks, real estate, really anything just imagine it and people will eat it up. They’re sheep, remember?
	- Step 2): Create product. Whether it’s an ebook, dvd’s, personal coaching whatever. My personal idea would be to build it up to a touring empire with conventions & DvD’s etc. the whole nine yards.
	- Step 3): You’ve already got the following to start the product, so give out prizes online or wherever to make people interested. Just spread the word, but make sure they believe you! Be very enthusiastic lol
	- MOST IMPORTANT STEP:
	- Step 4): Make people pass the word of mouth that you’re teaching them to get rich. And, you can change their lives if they just take a minute and listen. But, since everyone thinks everyone is a scammermake an incentivized program that if the person gets X number of friends to sign up they’ll get a $500 gift card or whatever you can give them.(People love money lol)

	- Step 5: Once large enough, and able to purchase ads then do it immediately!Television commercials/Google Adwords/radio are very effective at reaching the target audience.(the average joe)Invest in those venues of advertising to increase your capital(ROI), and get that message out like spam.
	- Step 6): Congratulations, you’re now a multi-millionaire.
	- Step 7): Rinse, repeat & grow larger and larger.
	- Extra tip: Invest in a PR clean up company for your product and name, because people will most likely Google search for things like “your product scam,” “your product reviews,” before they decide to buy so make damn sure there’s no loose ends.
	- This plan has been followed by many successful men, and it works.But why? Because people are sheep meant to be led.

	- I know you said you didn’t want to start a forum, but have you considered a private networking community like the Dynamite Circle:http://about.dynamitecircle.com/tmba/
	- It differs from a forum as people must meet minimum criteria before joining, and the focus is on making connections, both online and offline.
	- Your objection to a forum was it involves you doing all the work, but I know that isn’t the case with the Dyncamite Circle as they have community managers that run the whole thing:http://www.tropicalmba.com/WorkWithUs/(Scroll down to “Dynamite Circle Community Manager”)
	- They have “Hubs”, where large numbers of members who live nearby meet up on an ad hoc basis, “juntos” for monthly meetups. They also have an annual conference, and members can set up their own local conferences – called DCx, like TEDx.
	- It seems that by having a stringent application process (for the DC you need to have a business earning $5k/month) they filter out the riff raff which leads to a community where value is exchanged.

		- K says
	- April 21, 2015 at 6:47 pm
	- The best business idea for B&D would probably be to crowdsource business ideas from active readers in the form of a contest.
	- The people who comment are more likely to provide better ideas on how to improve B&D, since they’re your target audience, and essentially, future customers. The type of reader you attract is probably going to put in a little more work, otherwise why would they be visiting? Even if you don’t get any worthwhile ideas, it’s a way to get specific feedback to improve your business anyway. Either way, everyone benefits.
	- Offer a decent prize — enticing enough to elicit quality responses, but at the same time, just a drop in the bucket compared to the returns you’ll receive. Even the ideas that don’t win overall will still offer value: directly, by giving you something actionable and immediately profitable; or indirectly, by helping you develop new ideas in a more focused direction. You’re a business owner, you can outsource/get counsel for stuff like this and use your time/resources for something else.

		- Rali says
	- April 21, 2015 at 9:43 pm
	- DISCLAIMER: I do not know the demographics of your audience.
	- Clarify where you are in the ‘bell curve’ of customer acquisition by understanding who it is that you’re currently targeting and what group of people you want to target next.
	- Geoffrey A. Moore writes about this topic in his book ‘Crossing the Chasm’.
	- After your initial B&D innovation, comes the visionaries (the people that see your vision).
	- Then, there’s a large chasm that separates the visinaries from the mainstream market of early adopters.
	- Next, a small crack that separates early adopters from late adopters.
	- Finally, there’s the laggards (the absolute last people to adopt your material).
	- Your empire is fairly young so your market seems to be early male visionaries who are in need of a kickstart.
	- That’s 1/3 of your visionary market.
	- You own a large portion of a small pond. – That’s discussed in the book ‘Zero to One’ by Peter Thiel.
	- 2/3 Would be women. – Duplicate your current content and tailor it for visionary women.
	- 3/3 would be the children of the visionary men and women. – This will build a future of customers that trust your company. Eventually B&D will outgrow you.
	- If the men a women that currently value your content begin to teach your methods to their children, you have longevity.
	- Think of B&D as your Apple II.
	- You have iPod, MacBook Pro, iPhone, Mac Pro, iMax and so many more markets to cover in the future.
	- Pick a steering direction in order to capture more large portions of small markets and bring them together under B&D and create a solid ecosystem, much like Facebook.
	- (Facebook is separating into parts so at least a few of their products will always be used some way or another.)
	- DISCLAIMER: I don’t know where you’re trying to steer B&D.
	- BRANDING. You need distinctive logo. Something clear that translates what you do in a glance.
	- Plaster it everywhere so it becomes a staple.
	- As much guilt as I feel having an Apple logo pasted on all of my devices, I still love it. It’s adds a bit of reassurance to whatever I’m buying.
	- The female owner of Sleep America speaks about this topic on ‘Rich Dad Radio’.
	- She picked a logo and slogan and ran with for years so that any new product under the brand umbrella was trusted.
	- HINT HINT – She’s a female mogul that women would love to learn about.
	- TL;DR1. Continue to capture large portions of small markets by tailoring similar content for women and eventually their children. Don’t make it so drastically different that the men here wouldn’t want to read it too.
	- What you do now is working. Just double down on it for different types of people.
	- 2. BRANDING. BRANDING. BRANDING. LOGO. LOGO. LOGO.
	- 3. Find out where the transition chasm from visionary men and women to the mainstream early adopters is located and prepare.
	- 4. Read ‘Zero to One’ and ‘Chrossing the Chasm’
	- 5. Make a physical well packaged product with your logo stamped on it that isn’t a supplement, ebook or some type of expected product from a fitness / life coach. – Change the game.
	- All of this is easy in principle, as you know, ideas aren’t worth anything and execution is the trick.
	- Just some mental flexing.
	- – Rali

		- Michael Karner says
	- April 21, 2015 at 11:25 pm
	- Make your books Amazon Bestsellers and improve the global exposure of Bold And Determined
	- There’s a huge difference between selling books on Amazon and being an Amazon Bestseller
	- Here’s exactly how you do it:
	- 1. Upload e-book on amazon.com
	- 2. Optionally: upload e-book onto createspace.com and publish it as print paperback book (Createspace is an Amazon company, producing books via print-on-demand. A book is printed only when it’s ordered on Amazon and Createspace/Amazon takes care of shipping. No costs for the author/publisher.)
	- 3. The big thing: Set a pre-order period on amazon.com (I recommend 2-4 weeks) – here’s why: every sale you generate during pre-order period counts as sale on release-day. Amazon bestseller lists count sales per day, even hours. A couple hundred sales on one day (which in your case are generated over the whole pre-order time), bring your product into the Top 100 Amazon Bestseller List, a couple thousand in the Top 10.Once in the Bestseller List, Amazon will promote the product. On top of that, a huge exposure is guaranteed by being seen in the Bestseller List, where readers are shopping for books.Sub-categories are an additional help, which can be dominated completely. Each category of books as well as each sub-category has its own bestseller list.
	- 4. Get 100 reviews on amazon in pre-order period and have them on your amazon sales page on day one (1. Reviews from your already existing readers and/or 2. Reviews from new readers, especially bloggers you give the e-book version for free in exchange for a review)
	- 5. Additionally, during pre-order period I would run targeted Facebook advertisement to your target audience
	- 6. Long-term addition: get your print books into physical bookstores and have a presence in every important place around the globe
	- With the 500$ I will buy a ticket to Vietnam and work with you on this.
	- Best,Michael Karner

	- Create a B&D Motivational Digital Picture Frame.
	- Source the digital photo frames from a manufacturer in China. Compile a list of 100 of your favorite quotes. Hire a graphic designer to put those quotes to some nice background images. Then load those 100 images into the picture frame and sell it as a “Motivational Digital Picture Frame” Get BoldandDetermined.com printed on the frame as well for branding.

	- April 22, 2015 at 2:12 am
	- Possibly another winner came to mind. Create a test. This test is used to profile a consumer. It would be to used identify weaknesses in an individual. It is a test taken online and charged as a one-time only fee.
	- It can be used as a precursor to navigating your site. Perhaps, rather, a tool to point out things that are not so obvious to the reader. After all, no one can live the life of a wolf, thinking like a sheep.
	- The test itself would essentially be a personality assessment. Based on the answers, one would be given a customized assessment of their strengths and weaknesses, according to B&D standards. You could call it the Wolf Test, or whatever clever name you can think of.
	- The first thing you would do is create 20-50+ questions (the more questions asked, the more accurate the assessment). You set-up the answering format as multiple choice, or a number system that indicates how strongly someone feels about a statement or answer to a question (eg. 1-very strong, 2-strong, 3-somewhat, 4-not very strong, 5-not strong at all).
	- You can organize the questions into sections based on traits (eg. initiative, work ethic, practicality, etc.), but not reveal to the test taker why they are being asked certain questions (obviously). It is important to make the test specific to Bold & Determined. Otherwise, someone can simply go anywhere to get a personality assessment. This test should be created specifically to identify the wolves from the sheep and to point out to the sheep how to be wolves. This is done by linking people to specific products you sell (all of them!), or to affiliates that offer you commision for sending business their way.
	- The answers would be tallied using percentages. Each section scored using percents. Low percentages (below 70%) indicate traits that need to be strengthened, high percentages (70%+) indicate traits that are strong, but could be improved.
	- Just a thought. I always enjoyed personality tests. The accurate and reputable ones, that is. Many people do not, because tests tell you how it is, not how you would like it to be. Just as you do, Victor.
	- – Greg

		- Claudio says
	- April 22, 2015 at 2:17 am
	- Searching in Google for the articles on boldanddetermined.com I can see that all the descriptions of your articles since two years start with “From the desk of Victor Pride. Subj: ” and they contain a line “————”.This is because you haven’t set a meta-description tag in the html of your articles, so Google takes the content of your article and uses it as the default meta-description.The problem is that there are two rows that Google displays as a “teaser” to any link, and the two tokens above waste about 35% of that space, so anybody that is searching online for some information could be taken aback from clicking because it could not be so clear that there is quality content here.The solution is a little work but it could mean some more clicking (not indexing, meta description tags don’t influence it). Use a SEO module to convert the content of your articles in the meta-description tag REMOVING the tokens above, so you can have all quality content on your Google results.

		- Peter says
	- April 22, 2015 at 6:46 am
	- Hey Vic,
	- A lot of these ideas are great, but most of them require significant labor overhead from you. So here’s an idea that would require very little time from you once it’s up and running…
	- BAD Insider – I’m guessing you already have a sharp eye on business numbers with plenty of financial data at your fingertips. I’m also guessing that a good portion of your audience would salivate at the idea of seeing those numbers.
	- You could set up a paid monthly subscription where you let Insiders see numbers, trends, graphs, etc. from each income stream. You could provide insights into these numbers at your discretion, and give a short recap into what’s going on in the business. It would almost be a like a newsletter from a company to the shareholders (without all the corporate BS of course).
	- Since you probably already track these things, the main effort would be putting this in a nice, clean package (perhaps an HTML email or a PDF). You could pay someone to create an automated system that pulls various metrics (income, expenses, traffic, sales, etc.) into a sharp looking report, or you could simply hire someone to do this each month. Either way, YOUR only input would be directing this effort and providing business context (which is something you probably do anyway).
	- A lot of your readership has business mentality. Numbers help us make better business decisions, like predicting costs and seeing the most lucrative aspects of your business at any given time. Access to numbers from a big name in the game are invaluable.
	- This is a low risk venture with the potential for decent upside.
	- I think you could easily get 2-3% of your subscribers to pay $3/month for a subscription to BAD Insider. If you got just 1%, that’s 1900 x $3 x 12 = $6840/year for something that you can almost entirely automate. The main expenses would be initial development (or a few hours/month from a developer if you didn’t automate), and a few hours/month from you to oversee and provide high level insight.
	- In terms of traffic, you would attract a whole new demographic in addition to your normal readership.Suppose I don’t want to read a blog, but I’m a blogger myself and I want data to make better business decisions. I see that you’re a very successful blogger, so I become a paying subscriber without even reading one article just so I can see those numbers.
	- A lot of bloggers do this, but they half ass it. Smartpassiveincome.com does “Monthly Income Reports” for free and it attracts many readers. However, to me, the way he presents numbers is messy and not that helpful. In a giant block of text, it displays profits and expenses month over month, which doesn’t give you the big picture view. He also rambles about non-business matters in there too, which gets annoying. You would stand out big time if you made a better version of this.
	- I’d personally pay $10/mo for a professional report that shows rich detail, trends, and presents data cleanly with valuable insights so I can skim it and make sense of it. I’m confident that getting under the hood of the BAD empire would be a game changer, especially for newer bloggers.
	- -Peter

	- Victor,
	- I loved the emphasis on Business vs Self-Employment. Far too many people are afraid to let go and delegate.
	- I have a comment about Badwear’s presentation. It’s far too busy a page the way it is now. My first impression seeing all the clothing all over is “clutter”.
	- Because I know you are a disciplined, organized man, I know you have sales metrics for every product listed there. Use the Pareto principle (called the 80/20 rule by the uneducated) and put each category leader down as a header image that you can click through to get at the underachievers in the same category.
	- This will have the following advantages:
	- 1) You will be able to free up and allocate vastly more page space on the landing page (the only page most clickthroughs will ever see) to clothes that are already doing well. This should result in an immediate increase in sales.
	- 2) Your staff will be able to create a much cleaner, leaner overall look for the site. This is manly wear, so you don’t want it to resemble a collection of geeky crap like this: http://www.cafepress.com/+lollipop-guild+gifts
	- Here is a 30-second mockup I did you can hand to your website people and have them doll up:
	- http://i.imgur.com/bNiyCHW.png
	- I do solemnly swear that I will spend all $500 on booze, red meat, condoms and other essentials exclusively for myself.
	- Regards,Josh
	- p.s. Bonus comment: The brown leather boxing gloves at the bottom, though they do have old-school cachet, look almost exactly like dog turds when viewed on a screen <7" in size, a rapidly-growing demographic. Use red like I did or black, but please change it.

	- Some of these ideas are pretty decent and yes a mug will make you some sales but what you want to do is stop fishing for small fish.
	- Tony Robbins has events that are over $10,000 per. Some people are even willing to pay $25,000 and up for quality training.
	- But people may say oh I do not have that kind of expertise to charge that amount of money.
	- I give them the same advice I give to people that do not think they can write an eBook or create their first product. You simply become a compiler. Find the best information and training that is out there and create a unique resource from that information.
	- Think about it. You do not even have to be a speaker you can recruit others to offer the training in their unique fields and you as the coordinator will still make a small mint.
	- Google Jay Abraham and he has alot of free resources and Ytube videos to tap into. I mean he can make millions by simply brokering deals with one business with a huge mailing list to another business with a great product and all 3 make a killing in profits.
	- This stuff is not hard!
	- Expand your mind and decrease self limiting beliefs.
	- Offer VALUE and that value can easily be some other experts that YOU give an audience to and you both end up crushing it.

	- April 22, 2015 at 9:31 pm
	- Here’s my B&D residual profit idea:
	- THE CURRENT SITUATION:People visit B&D for articles, branded purchases or advice, in particular weight training for back and legs as they are big muscle groups, and weight training for these muscle groups require equipment, such as a weight lifting belt. B&D branded weight training equipment, such as a weight lifting belt, currently does not exist. Also, not everyone in every gym knows about B&D (I asked in mine).
	- THE IDEAL SITUATION:When people visit B&D for articles, branded purchases or advice, in particular weight training for back and legs as they are big muscle groups, they will see a B&D branded weight lifting belt, which can be purchased. Also, it would be designed to ‘work’ for B&D so that everyone in every gym knows about B&D.
	- THE EFFORT REQUIRED:A reasonably short and one-off period of time would be required to design and produce the belt with the intention of it being simple and non-complicated, while clearly showing on the back section of the belt (facing outwards) the B&D logo, and underneath the logo, the URL http://www.boldanddetermined.com is displayed.
	- There is also the option for different versions of the belt, i.e. same design but different logo and URL to promote it. Therefore, one belt design for B&D, one for BADWEAR, one for 30 Days of Discipline etc.
	- THE RESIDUAL PROFIT:People who already know about B&D and visit it, can buy it. They will then wear it at the gym, and as the logo and URL are on the outside face of the belt, other people will see it, and end up looking up the URL sooner or later (you’ll be surprised how many people are looking at their phones in the gym), and eventually reading articles and making purchases.
	- It is also residual marketing, as the belt design promotes the logo and URL. As Vic once said in one of his articles about marketing, having a good product is actually ‘good’ marketing. The logo and URL would be in every one’s visual eye line so it is automatic exposure.
	- Now imagine everyone in the gym seeing one of these… then every gym in the town… then every town in the state… then every state in the country… then every country in the world.
	- If this becomes the winning concept, the money will be kept and invested in a way that makes more money.
